OUT\n    29→        floating[::1] upper_bounds,                    # OUT\n    30→        floating[:, ::1] lower_bounds,                 # OUT\n    31→        int n_threads):\n    32→    \"\"\"Initialize upper and lower bounds for each sample for dense input data.\n    33→\n    34→    Given X, centers and the pairwise distances divided by 2.0 between the\n    35→    centers this calculates the upper bounds and lower bounds for each sample.\n    36→    The upper bound for each sample is set to the distance between the sample\n    37→    and the closest center.\n    38→\n    39→    The lower bound for each sample is a one-dimensional array of n_clusters.\n    40→    For each sample i assume that the previously assigned cluster is c1 and the\n    41→    previous closest distance is dist, for a new cluster c2, the\n    42→    lower_bound[i][c2] is set to distance between the sample and this new\n    43→    cluster, if and only if dist > center_half_distances[c1][c2]. This prevents\n    44→    computation of unnecessary distances for each sample to the clusters that\n    45→    it is unlikely to be assigned to.\n    46→\n    47→    Parameters\n    48→    ----------\n    49→    X : ndarray of shape (n_samples, n_features), dtype=floating\n    50→        The input data.\n    51→\n    52→    centers : ndarray of shape (n_clusters, n_features), dtype=floating\n    53→        The cluster centers.\n    54→\n    55→    center_half_distances : ndarray of shape (n_clusters, n_clusters), \\\n    56→            dtype=floating\n    57→        The half of the distance between any 2 clusters centers.\n    58→\n    59→    labels : ndarray of shape(n_samples), dtype=int\n    60→        The label for each sample. This array is modified in place.\n    61→\n    62→    upper_bounds : ndarray of shape(n_samples,), dtype=floating\n    63→        The upper bound on the distance between each sample and its closest\n    64→        cluster center. This array is modified in place.\n    65→\n    66→    lower_bounds : ndarray, of shape(n_samples, n_clusters), dtype=floating\n    67→        The lower bound on the distance between each sample and each cluster\n    68→        center. This array is modified in place.\n    69→\n    70→    n_threads : int\n    71→        The number of threads to be used by openmp.\n    72→    \"\"\"\n    73→    cdef:\n    74→        int n_samples = X.shape[0]\n    75→        int n_clusters = centers.shape[0]\n    76→        int n_features = X.shape[1]\n    77→\n    78→        floating min_dist, dist\n    79→        int best_cluster, i, j\n    80→\n    81→    for i in prange(\n    82→        n_samples, num_threads=n_threads, schedule='static', nogil=True\n    83→    ):\n    84→        best_cluster = 0\n    85→        min_dist = _euclidean_dense_dense(&X[i, 0], &centers[0, 0],\n    86→                                          n_features, False)\n    87→        lower_bounds[i, 0] = min_dist\n    88→        for j in range(1, n_clusters):\n    89→            if min_dist > center_half_distances[best_cluster, j]:\n    90→                dist = _euclidean_dense_dense(&X[i, 0], &centers[j, 0],\n    91→                                              n_features, False)\n    92→                lower_bounds[i, j] = dist\n    93→                if dist < min_dist:\n    94→                    min_dist = dist\n    95→                    best_cluster = j\n    96→        labels[i] = best_cluster\n    97→        upper_bounds[i] = min_dist\n    98→\n    99→\n   100→def init_bounds_sparse(\n   101→        X,                                             # This prevents\n   120→    computation of unnecessary distances for each sample to the clusters that\n   121→    it is unlikely to be assigned to.\n   122→\n   123→    Parameters\n   124→    ----------\n   125→    X : sparse matrix of shape (n_samples, n_features), dtype=floating\n   126→        The input data. Must be in CSR format.\n   127→\n   128→    centers : ndarray of shape (n_clusters, n_features), dtype=floating\n   129→        The cluster centers.\n   130→\n   131→    center_half_distances : ndarray of shape (n_clusters, n_clusters), \\\n   132→            dtype=floating\n   133→        The half of the distance between any 2 clusters centers.\n   134→\n   135→    labels : ndarray of shape(n_samples), dtype=int\n   136→        The label for each sample. This array is modified in place.\n   137→\n   138→    upper_bounds : ndarray of shape(n_samples,), dtype=floating\n   139→        The upper bound on the distance between each sample and its closest\n   140→        cluster center. This array is modified in place.\n   141→\n   142→    lower_bounds : ndarray of shape(n_samples, n_clusters), dtype=floating\n   143→        The lower bound on the distance between each sample and each cluster\n   144→        center. 185→\n   186→def elkan_iter_chunked_dense(\n   187→        const floating[:, ::1] X,                      # IN\n   188→        const floating[::1] sample_weight,             # IN\n   189→        const floating[:, ::1] centers_old,            # IN\n   190→        floating[:, ::1] centers_new,                  # OUT\n   191→        floating[::1] weight_in_clusters,              # OUT\n   192→        const floating[:, ::1] center_half_distances,  # IN\n   193→        const floating[::1] distance_next_center,      # IN\n   194→        floating[::1] upper_bounds,                    # INOUT\n   195→        floating[:, ::1] lower_bounds,                 # INOUT\n   196→        int[::1] labels,                               # INOUT\n   197→        floating[::1] center_shift,                    # OUT\n   198→        int n_threads,\n   199→        bint update_centers=True):\n   200→    \"\"\"Single iteration of K-means Elkan algorithm with dense input.\n   201→\n   202→    Update labels and centers (inplace), for one iteration, distributed\n   203→    over data chunks.\n   204→\n   205→    Parameters\n   206→    ----------\n   207→    X : ndarray of shape (n_samples, n_features), dtype=floating\n   208→        The observations to cluster.\n   209→\n   210→    sample_weight : ndarray of shape (n_samples,), dtype=floating\n   211→        The weights for each observation in X.\n   212→\n   213→    centers_old : ndarray of shape (n_clusters, n_features), dtype=floating\n   214→        Centers before previous iteration, placeholder for the centers after\n   215→        previous  computed during this iteration.\n   220→\n   221→    weight_in_clusters : ndarray of shape (n_clusters,), dtype=floating\n   222→        Placeholder for the sums of the weights of every observation assigned\n   223→        to each center.\n   224→\n   225→    center_half_distances : ndarray of shape (n_clusters, n_clusters), \\\n   226→            dtype=floating\n   227→        Half pairwise distances between centers.\n   228→\n   229→    distance_next_center : ndarray of shape (n_clusters,), dtype=floating\n   230→        Distance between each center its closest center.\n   231→\n   232→    upper_bounds : ndarray of shape (n_samples,), dtype=floating\n   233→        Upper bound for the distance between each sample and its center,\n   234→        updated inplace.\n   235→\n   236→    lower_bounds : ndarray of shape (n_samples, n_clusters), dtype=floating\n   237→        Lower bound for the distance between each sample and each center,\n   238→        updated inplace.\n   239→\n between old and new centers.\n   245→\n   246→    n_threads : int\n   247→        The number of threads to be used by openmp.\n   248→\n   249→    update_centers : bool\n   250→        - If True, the of\n   253→          the algorithm. This is useful especially when calling predict on a\n   254→          fitted model.\n   255→    \"\"\"\n   256→    cdef:\n   257→        int n_samples = X.shape[0]\n   258→        int n_features = X.shape[1]\n   259→        int n_clusters = centers_new.shape[0]\n   260→\n   261→    if n_samples == 0:\n   262→        # An empty array was passed, do nothing and return early (before\n   263→        # attempting to compute n_chunks). This can typically happen when\n   264→        # calling the prediction function of a bisecting k-means model with a\n   265→        # large fraction of outliers.\n   266→        return\n   267→\n   268→    cdef:\n   269→        # hard-coded number of samples per chunk. IN\n        const floating[:, ::1] centers,                # IN\n        const floating[:, ::1] center_half_distances,  # IN\n        int[::1] labels,                               # OUT\n        floating[::1] upper_bounds,                    # OUT\n        floating[:, ::1] lower_bounds,                 # OUT\n        int n_threads):\n    \"\"\"Initialize upper and lower bounds for each sample for dense input data.\n\n    Given X, centers and the pairwise distances divided by 2.0 between the\n    centers this calculates the upper bounds and lower bounds for each sample.\n    The upper bound for each sample is set to the distance between the sample\n    and the closest center.\n\n    The lower bound for each sample is a one-dimensional array of n_clusters.\n    For each sample i assume that the previously assigned cluster is c1 and the\n    previous closest distance is dist, for a new cluster c2, the\n    lower_bound[i][c2] is set to distance between the sample and this new\n    cluster, if and only if dist > center_half_distances[c1][c2]. This prevents\n    computation of unnecessary distances for each sample to the clusters that\n    it is unlikely to be assigned to.\n\n    Parameters\n    ----------\n    X : ndarray of shape (n_samples, n_features), dtype=floating\n        The input data.\n\n    centers : ndarray of shape (n_clusters, n_features), dtype=floating\n        The cluster centers.\n\n    center_half_distances : ndarray of shape (n_clusters, n_clusters), \\\n            dtype=floating\n        The half of the distance between any 2 clusters centers.\n\n    labels : ndarray of shape(n_samples), dtype=int\n        The label for each sample. This array is modified in place.\n\n    upper_bounds : ndarray of shape(n_samples,), dtype=floating\n        The upper bound on the distance between each sample and its closest\n        cluster center. This array is modified in place.\n\n    lower_bounds : ndarray, of shape(n_samples, n_clusters), dtype=floating\n        The lower bound on the distance between each sample and each cluster\n        center. OUT\n        floating[:, ::1] lower_bounds,                 # OUT\n        int n_threads):\n    \"\"\"Initialize upper and lower bounds for each sample for sparse input data.\n\n    Given X, centers and the pairwise distances divided by 2.0 between the\n    centers this calculates the upper bounds and lower bounds for each sample.\n    The upper bound for each sample is set to the distance between the sample\n    and the closest center.\n\n    The lower bound for each sample is a one-dimensional array of n_clusters.\n    For each sample i assume that the previously assigned cluster is c1 and the\n    previous closest distance is dist, for a new cluster c2, the\n    lower_bound[i][c2] is set to distance between the sample and this new\n    cluster, if and only if dist > center_half_distances[c1][c2]. This prevents\n    computation of unnecessary distances for each sample to the clusters that\n    it is unlikely to be assigned to.\n\n    Parameters\n    ----------\n    X : sparse matrix of shape (n_samples, n_features), dtype=floating\n        The input data. Must be in CSR format.\n\n    centers : ndarray of shape (n_clusters, n_features), dtype=floating\n        The cluster centers.\n\n    center_half_distances : ndarray of shape (n_clusters, n_clusters), \\\n            dtype=floating\n        The half of the distance between any 2 clusters centers.\n\n    labels : ndarray of shape(n_samples), dtype=int\n        The label for each sample. This array is modified in place.\n\n    upper_bounds : ndarray of shape(n_samples,), dtype=floating\n        The upper bound on the distance between each sample and its closest\n        cluster center. This array is modified in place.\n\n    lower_bounds : ndarray of shape(n_samples, n_clusters), dtype=floating\n        The lower bound on the distance between each sample and each cluster\n        center. This array is modified in place.\n\n    n_threads : int\n        The number of threads to be used by openmp.\n    \"\"\"\n    cdef:\n        int n_samples = X.shape[0]\n        int n_clusters = centers.shape[0]\n\n        floating[::1] X_data = X.data\n        int[::1] X_indices = X.indices\n        int[::1] X_indptr = X.indptr\n\n        floating min_dist, dist\n        int best_cluster, i, j\n\n        floating[::1] centers_squared_norms = row_norms(centers, squared=True)\n\n    for i in prange(\n        n_samples, num_threads=n_threads, schedule='static', nogil=True\n    ):\n        best_cluster = 0\n        min_dist = _euclidean_sparse_dense(\n            X_data[X_indptr[i]: X_indptr[i + 1]],\n            X_indices[X_indptr[i]: X_indptr[i + 1]],\n            centers[0], centers_squared_norms[0], False)\n\n        lower_bounds[i, 0] = min_dist\n        for j in range(1, n_clusters):\n            if min_dist > center_half_distances[best_cluster, j]:\n                dist = _euclidean_sparse_dense(\n                    X_data[X_indptr[i]: X_indptr[i + 1]],\n                    X_indices[X_indptr[i]: X_indptr[i + 1]],\n                    centers[j], centers_squared_norms[j], False)\n                lower_bounds[i, j] = dist\n                if dist < min_dist:\n                    min_dist = dist\n                    best_cluster = j\n        labels[i] = best_cluster\n        upper_bounds[i] = min_dist\n\n\ndef elkan_iter_chunked_dense(\n        const floating[:, ::1] X,                      # IN\n        const floating[::1] sample_weight,             # IN\n        const floating[:, ::1] centers_old,            # IN\n        floating[:, ::1] centers_new,                  # OUT\n        floating[::1] weight_in_clusters,              # OUT\n        const floating[:, ::1] center_half_distances,  # IN\n        const floating[::1] distance_next_center,      # IN\n        floating[::1] upper_bounds,                    # INOUT\n        floating[:, ::1] lower_bounds,                 # INOUT\n        int[::1] labels,                               # INOUT\n        floating[::1] center_shift,                    # OUT\n        int n_threads,\n        bint update_centers=True):\n    \"\"\"Single iteration of K-means Elkan algorithm with dense input.\n\n    Update labels and centers (inplace), for one iteration, distributed\n    over data chunks.\n\n    Parameters\n    ----------\n    X : ndarray of shape (n_samples, n_features), dtype=floating\n        The observations to cluster.\n\n    sample_weight : ndarray of shape (n_samples,), dtype=floating\n        The weights for each observation in X.\n\n    centers_old : ndarray of shape (n_clusters, n_features), dtype=floating\n        Centers before previous iteration, placeholder for the centers after\n        previous iteration.\n\n    centers_new : ndarray of shape (n_clusters, n_features), dtype=floating\n        Centers after previous iteration, placeholder for the new centers\n        computed during this iteration.\n\n    weight_in_clusters : ndarray of shape (n_clusters,), dtype=floating\n        Placeholder for the sums of the weights of every observation assigned\n        to each center.\n\n    center_half_distances : ndarray of shape (n_clusters, n_clusters), \\\n            dtype=floating\n        Half pairwise distances between centers.\n\n    distance_next_center : ndarray of shape (n_clusters,), dtype=floating\n        Distance between each center its closest center.\n\n    upper_bounds : ndarray of shape (n_samples,), This can typically happen when\n        # calling the prediction function of a bisecting k-means model with a\n        # large fraction of outliers.\n        return\n\n    cdef:\n        # hard-coded number of samples per chunk. Splitting in chunks is\n        # necessary to get parallelism. OUT\n   363→        bint update_centers) noexcept nogil:\n   364→    \"\"\"K-means combined EM step for one dense data chunk.\n   365→\n   366→    Compute the partial contribution of a single data chunk to the labels and\n   367→    centers.\n   368→    \"\"\"\n   369→    cdef:\n   370→        int n_samples = labels.shape[0]\n   371→        int n_clusters = centers_old.shape[0]\n   372→        int n_features = centers_old.shape[1]\n   373→\n   374→        floating upper_bound, distance\n   375→        int i, j, k, label\n   376→\n   377→    for i in range(n_samples):\n   378→        upper_bound = upper_bounds[i]\n   379→        bounds_tight = 0\n   380→        label = labels[i]\n   381→\n   382→        # OUT\n        floating[:, ::1] lower_bounds,                 # OUT\n        int n_threads):\n    \"\"\"Initialize upper and lower bounds for each sample for dense input data.\n\n    Given X, centers and the pairwise distances divided by 2.0 between the\n    centers this calculates the upper bounds and lower bounds for each sample.\n    The upper bound for each sample is set to the distance between the sample\n    and the closest center.\n\n    The lower bound for each sample is a one-dimensional array of n_clusters.\n    For each sample i assume that the previously assigned cluster is c1 and the\n    previous closest distance is dist, for a new cluster c2, the\n    lower_bound[i][c2] is set to distance between the sample and this new\n    cluster, if and only if dist > center_half_distances[c1][c2]. This prevents\n    computation of unnecessary distances for each sample to the clusters that\n    it is unlikely to be assigned to.\n\n    Parameters\n    ----------\n    X : ndarray of shape (n_samples, n_features), dtype=floating\n        The input data.\n\n    centers : ndarray of shape (n_clusters, n_features), dtype=floating\n        The cluster centers.\n\n    center_half_distances : ndarray of shape (n_clusters, n_clusters), \\\n            dtype=floating\n        The half of the distance between any 2 clusters centers.\n\n    labels : ndarray of shape(n_samples), dtype=int\n        The label for each sample. This array is modified in place.\n\n    upper_bounds : ndarray of shape(n_samples,), dtype=floating\n        The upper bound on the distance between each sample and its closest\n        cluster center. OUT\n        floating[:, ::1] lower_bounds,                 # OUT\n        int n_threads):\n    \"\"\"Initialize upper and lower bounds for each sample for sparse input data.\n\n    Given X, centers and the pairwise distances divided by 2.0 between the\n    centers this calculates the upper bounds and lower bounds for each sample.\n    The upper bound for each sample is set to the distance between the sample\n    and the closest center.\n\n    The lower bound for each sample is a one-dimensional array of n_clusters.\n    For each sample i assume that the previously assigned cluster is c1 and the\n    previous closest distance is dist, for a new cluster c2, the\n    lower_bound[i][c2] is set to distance between the sample and this new\n    cluster, if and only if dist > center_half_distances[c1][c2]. {"type":"assistant","message":{"model":"claude-haiku-4-5-20251001","id":"msg_01GqAKhqfEy7dzydBz75juy9","type":"message","role":"assistant","content":[{"type":"thinking","thinking":"Wait, this optimization is also not right. I'm computing the upper bound potentially when I don't need to, because I'm checking in a preliminary loop whether `need_tight_bounds` is true, but then I'm still doing the same check in the main loop.\n\nActually, looking at the original code more carefully, the logic is:\n1. First check: `if (j != label and (upper_bound > lower_bounds[i, j]) and (upper_bound > center_half_distances[label, j]))`\n   - This decides if we should enter the block\n2. Inside the block, if `not bounds_tight`, compute the actual distance to label\n3. Then check: `if (upper_bound > lower_bounds[i, j] or (upper_bound > center_half_distances[label, j]))`\n   - The OR is needed because the upper_bound might have changed!\n4. If that passes, compute the actual distance to j\n\nThe key issue is that the computation of the tight upper bound happens inside the loop over j, and only if the first check passed. This means we might compute it multiple times if multiple clusters pass the first check.\n\nThe optimization I was trying to do is: compute the tight bound once before the loop if ANY cluster might need it, then we don't need the `if not bounds_tight` check inside the loop.\n\nBut wait, that's not quite right either, because the tight upper bound should only be computed if it will actually be used.\n\nHmm, let me think about this differently. The current algorithm:\n1. For each sample i:\n   - Initialize upper_bound from previous iteration\n   - For each cluster j != label:\n     - If `upper_bound > lower_bounds[i, j] AND upper_bound > center_half_distances[label, j]`:\n       - If bounds_tight is false, compute tight upper_bound (distance to label)\n       - If `upper_bound > lower_bounds[i, j] OR upper_bound > center_half_distances[label, j]`:\n         - Compute distance to j and update if closer\n\nThe inefficiency is that we might compute the tight upper bound multiple times if several clusters pass the initial checks. But we can't precompute it outside the loop entirely since we only need it if at least one cluster satisfies the conditions. Maybe I should compute it once on first use and then reuse it for subsequent clusters in that iteration.\n\nLet me look at the actual code structure more carefully. In lines 399-403, the tight bounds computation happens inside the outer condition check but outside the nested one. The pattern is: if j passes the first set of conditions, then check if we need tight bounds, and only compute them once per point. After that, the tight bound gets reused for any other clusters that also pass those same initial conditions.\n\nThis lazy evaluation is already fairly efficient since it avoids unnecessary computation. Other potential improvements could include better memory access patterns, SIMD operations for batch distance calculations, or early stopping if a sufficiently close cluster is found.\n\nFor early termination, once we identify a closer cluster and tighten the upper_bound, we could check if remaining clusters have any chance of being nearer. This would need tracking the minimum lower_bound across unprocessed clusters, though the overhead might outweigh the benefit.\n\nThe current approach already re-evaluates both conditions after tightening the bound, which helps filter out more candidates. The key is that the second check becomes more effective once upper_bound decreases. the logic checks out. After tightening the bounds, the upper_bound decreases, so the second condition might now fail even though it passed before.\n\nI could reduce memory accesses by reordering clusters based on their lower bounds to prioritize promising candidates first, but sorting adds overhead. Let me reconsider the logic:\n\nOriginal code:\n```\nif (j != label and (upper_bound > lower_bounds[i, j]) and (upper_bound > center_half_distances[label, j])):\n    if not bounds_tight:\n        upper_bound = ...\n    if (upper_bound > lower_bounds[i, j] or (upper_bound > center_half_distances[label, j])):\n        distance = ...\n```\n\nMy patch changed it to:\n```\nif (j != label and (upper_bound > lower_bounds[i, j])):\n    if upper_bound <= center_half_distances[label, j]:\n        continue\n    if bounds_tight == 0:\n        upper_bound = ...\n    if upper_bound > lower_bounds[i, j]:\n        distance = ...\n```\n\nThe issue with my change:\n1. I'm now computing the distance only if `upper_bound > lower_bounds[i, j]`\n2. But the original OR condition allowed computing distance even if the lower_bounds check failed, as long as the triangle inequality check passed\n3. This changes the algorithm!\n\nActually, let me reconsider the logic again. The two checks mean:\n- `upper_bound > lower_bounds[i, j]`: We haven't proven that j is too far away\n- `upper_bound > center_half_distances[label, j]`: The triangle inequality doesn't rule it out\n\nThese are two different ways to rule out j. The OR means: compute distance if either one hasn't ruled it out.\n\nBut after computing the actual distance to label (if bounds_tight was 0), the upper_bound becomes tighter. Then:\n- The lower_bounds[i, j] hasn't changed\n- The center_half_distances hasn't changed\n- So if `upper_bound > lower_bounds[i, j]` was false before, it's still false after (since upper_bound only decreased)\n\n\n- The same logic applies to the triangle inequality check—once upper_bound shrinks, it can't suddenly satisfy a condition it failed before.\n\nSo the second OR is actually redundant! If `upper_bound > lower_bounds[i, j]` is false, we don't compute. If it's true, we might compute depending on the triangle inequality check.\n\nSo simplifying to just `if upper_bound > lower_bounds[i, j]` is incorrect! We need to keep the OR or the triangle inequality check. The correct optimization should preserve both conditions or find a way to eliminate one that's truly redundant after the bounds tighten.","signature":"EuQTCkYICxgCKkB2ZBiCRcSrx/BPJ+RI9YN7HlgDy6ZnFHGT0j6MFMtiMeJ8WhkVtvK2zTb6yBIgyW/zdqTM5yigbscVkDTUQhiPEgyu2iuFKtC1u7hQmnIaDANBtyk5uZB9GDQlISIwTOwHx4a4h6v9NWClw26coe/3rhwohP42BULUSSB5c1pPe0vaAnMqUpg5LPTROeHLKssSf1s/H7CZhdnZQjcalt6pPN1HVuJG/el8hICLc6Un0mX1FaWdxuAWWsdqJvm4pK6F9UZa0QuxZX//BqLKSyUvZmLH5JpBbkva7NyJYEHG+Jt9Z9zvqNIu3WH9FWj4hW4bcG6vlVAptLSyqqdjq1gVLkRZlSx2w4QfPqhsmI5WaBVOt6ZAxqsJpHg2FlINK2jsxGnNZN3zrxuvzlYK6yR7Wc+HRSuO2FUuD3KECvPFNua+EMAqKCrrq2usgyzc4jVby/04oQrrACMR9Z78thDDtItIBr9Vjt/LR3UEq9XhH3koYC0+5Rlc2hWRJyKQyCZS0vS2ejC+lJrYQN3gv6QOT8uzLeNTTsaNdbiyhcZKKCnRTjSIV5fiXgm13CCGFJ3L0feptTAbMGpEvTkEjkFPgNTHzRDbCqLKrEn84k5edbB5ptbxHgy5nyU5kcWXbZ5Je1ZcofrpmTkOEotTodOSmxuXUFvsdRsgULMKOU9fPdVPPZfsQck8xx28cLlDTgh21ifpbVwFeTdoI/ChGYvbVSHoborcSNlr3mkrfWYrKo6eec1Go1A6dzZAUlU5BYvIoGjYvyBpiNKGmdbSKFqUaCdd/jBKobLmJ0ZH0o1gCgFo4la8+hqXU/OcXZHK98udo7MdhqyX4cGJEDw4LoCrqqRUs6OfIRQV6TdCSQOk926vbjCLUHrCK8/cS1Lgt8vaZgmZQByNB3gixj+oY1o24Ki9p5Gqy9/ufh3vlX7v+CPEHnQ19K4DP+gowVkO0I1TOIIdgyb2YllPAJtrml+Bhle/zxKLY8eEWWYgqiA62XH2PckJrdgd4KtdOQZzawavtiHXwbzbHV5ZuzenesxQCEk9GYIhbH7uHWulAWSc7/6r64QsVfP2vF1M4jPDZhu+vQOom4qoYXbxF7XQ9NlJ3TQnX1WP0hteF6UraG17jI710771w4ErB9+vpyeRbt1Nfl0M5e/XFqpILj1HuYbgbRWtmz28qj4F4m0gGNJ3F+waXOWCRKUcQRnT+d2sfMUeFwKv/Nbjgb4eiDMjXu7xWdx71gjBhYfviQv+vW20WYqmdFbn4Gln+JBgpqWsmIY3qIi+flCfxQQdXdW6hdZ69e0Jrho6BU5KOkoPO0nsWZWfauil2RbB75lJ0dPvbRM2WaFsA2N38xV0KPL0/RAuoy0fVfDJw1RZxxwYnzuy0dy/fjD5EWV7koo017sy9ofz6YHgUQqvHdlbiNNm3PxXmm5/1am8t54i/GNib2a4YSWy3IhZMe5af84SVH2FjS+k5wrtG+dH0t3yMt74muk8pA7r5J/clMVV4MB8s4f/O6blz+Srxd272miFcFwdXqDxDft4i6hbkjBiXWIoZGMUlNKxrCIfBn5Qp3VAHDAmTtAGh0ePyPixj6mI/cHM0iD8cwryJF1i3ueHXAz02uHxfPsPf+xVYW4uWUNZlUZ1ojER/DkVPl4p2C9nkuFBNJ9B/rNwuDutPMh7LG8tfRDHgXO4oT2G5I+EassXcUfUvPgp6ZwV1pBpq0rxJUDzwtMNQNw8YnlJnsJ7tkKxz5s/S8kd9Tweb1TWnI64HE4rN8Cy7Ek8JucuQ2LPsBCxkSgAhakS9yF2KMH7e5g2VaPZ7b+zvuC7x1UFbgORAGe862OvLBOKQ8BK8MI2ciqObf1mGSNqe1hRpiktl0KYZvthpuU6XRpiZS9NN3eT14vo1UKMyEVLvQZquU3Ai2cL/7O5Vb0wXw88lLzXjfphP1vJtQujUQ0TIEfqUB//KNyBh
